          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

          margin: auto;

          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }

        }

          flex-grow: 0;

          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);

          overflow-y: auto;

          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }

          }

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>

        <p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

I tried to repro using given instructions (as well as building an asan build locally, and symbolizing via valgrind instructions[1]). Through both approaches, I wasn't able to correctly symbolize and see function calls in stack traces, though it did reliably crash, and did fail to crash if I disabled MojoJS.



<span class="line"><!---->I tried to repro using given instructions (as well as building an asan build locally, and symbolizing via valgrind instructions[1]). Through both approaches, I wasn't able to correctly symbolize and see function calls in stack traces, though it did reliably crash, and did fail to crash if I disabled MojoJS.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Instead, I saw could once see a crash from a blink FontCache CHECK[2] failing. Other times, I'd see crashes with various LOG(ERROR) logs, often with something related to fonts. I wonder if this is some interesting interaction between clipboard and fonts?



<span class="line"><!---->Instead, I saw could once see a crash from a blink FontCache CHECK[2] failing. Other times, I'd see crashes with various LOG(ERROR) logs, often with something related to fonts. I wonder if this is some interesting interaction between clipboard and fonts?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





work38thaxus@, do you know if you can see the call stack for the crash? Or how what I can do to see this myself? Thanks!



<span class="line"><!---->work38thaxus@, do you know if you can see the call stack for the crash? Or how what I can do to see this myself? Thanks!<!----></span>

Hi.



<span class="line"><!---->Hi.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I used ASAN build, but I also could not able to correctly symbolize and see function calls in stack traces. (I could not see ASAN report correctly)



<span class="line"><!---->I used ASAN build, but I also could not able to correctly symbolize and see function calls in stack traces. (I could not see ASAN report correctly)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In my opinion, sometimes after executing ui::Clipboard X11::X11 Details::WaitAndGetTargetsList(ui::Clipboard Buffer), the value of rsp becomes invalid, and subsequent function calls may fail.



<span class="line"><!---->In my opinion, sometimes after executing ui::Clipboard X11::X11 Details::WaitAndGetTargetsList(ui::Clipboard Buffer), the value of rsp becomes invalid, and subsequent function calls may fail.<!----></span>



<br>





Maybe this caused ASAN to not work properly.



<span class="line"><!---->Maybe this caused ASAN to not work properly.<!----></span>



<br>

Thank you, work38thaxus@. The memo.log is very interesting... I suspect some issue with re-entrancy regarding ui::Clipboard X11::X11 Details::WaitAndGetTargetsList(ui::Clipboard Buffer)... I recall seeing bugs[1][2][3] and crashes like that in the past, where the X11 message loop would have some sort of issue that led to crashes...

Actually, I don't think that a segfault is usually classified as a security bug, since I'm not sure how this could be exploited to achieve remote code execution or view extra resources (though this certainly should be a stability bug). Does this sound right? If so, we should remove the ReleaseBlock-Stable and Security_Severity tags.

To give a bit more information,  the issue here seems to be that, when quickly/repeatedly calling[1] the mojo ClipboardHost's readText function[2], we hit a re-entrancy segfault crash somewhere in ui::Clipboard X11::X11 Details::WaitAndGetTargetsList(ui::Clipboard Buffer)[3], possibly from multiple instances calling this at once.



<span class="line"><!---->To give a bit more information,  the issue here seems to be that, when quickly/repeatedly calling[1] the mojo ClipboardHost's readText function[2], we hit a re-entrancy segfault crash somewhere in ui::Clipboard X11::X11 Details::WaitAndGetTargetsList(ui::Clipboard Buffer)[3], possibly from multiple instances calling this at once.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1]: See poc.html in description



<span class="line"><!---->[1]: See poc.html in description<!----></span>

#13: "Segmentation fault" (SIGSEGV) is an unhelpful x86 term for invalid memory access.



<span class="line"><!---->#13: "Segmentation fault" (SIGSEGV) is an unhelpful x86 term for invalid memory access.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Invalid memory accesses are generally security issues. They suggest that we're setting some pointer to an incorrect value, so the code setting the pointer isn't working as intended. This opens up the possibility that an attacker may be able to get control of the pointer's value, and cause memory accesses to a controlled address.



<span class="line"><!---->Invalid memory accesses are generally security issues. They suggest that we're setting some pointer to an incorrect value, so the code setting the pointer isn't working as intended. This opens up the possibility that an attacker may be able to get control of the pointer's value, and cause memory accesses to a controlled address.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If we're sure the Clipboard code around the impacted area hasn't changed in a long time, this doesn't need to be release-blocking. Before clearing that flag, let's make sure we vetted any recent changes.



<span class="line"><!---->If we're sure the Clipboard code around the impacted area hasn't changed in a long time, this doesn't need to be release-blocking. Before clearing that flag, let's make sure we vetted any recent changes.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If we're sure the bug is entirely within X11 and we're not misusing the API in any way, then we can consider removing the Security labels.



<span class="line"><!---->If we're sure the bug is entirely within X11 and we're not misusing the API in any way, then we can consider removing the Security labels.<!----></span>

#15: Would it make sense to build a queue for the mojo calls?



<span class="line"><!---->#15: Would it make sense to build a queue for the mojo calls?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Possible strategies:



<span class="line"><!---->Possible strategies:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1) While the underlying platform call executes, all incoming Read*() callbacks are queued. When the platform call completes, all callbacks are invoked with the same result.



<span class="line"><!---->1) While the underlying platform call executes, all incoming Read*() callbacks are queued. When the platform call completes, all callbacks are invoked with the same result.<!----></span>



<br>





2) Read*() calls are queued and executed in order.



<span class="line"><!---->2) Read*() calls are queued and executed in order.<!----></span>



<br>





3) Incoming Read*() calls are dropped while an underlying platform call is already underway.



<span class="line"><!---->3) Incoming Read*() calls are dropped while an underlying platform call is already underway.<!----></span>

Re: 



<span class="line"><!---->Re: <!----></span>





Comment 16



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c16"><!---->Comment 16<!----></a>





: Oops, thanks for the clarification around segfaults and security. 



<span class="line"><!---->: Oops, thanks for the clarification around segfaults and security. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I don't think clipboard threading/calls have been changed much, and vetted recent changes to confirm this. Recent (last 9 months) changes around this codepath (mojo readText -> x11's WaitAndGetTargetsList) mostly just involve refactoring of: X11 atoms[1], DLP[2][3][4]. Changes that make functional changes but shouldn't affect threading include  x11 selection checks[5], or adding metrics for clipboard writes[6].



<span class="line"><!---->I don't think clipboard threading/calls have been changed much, and vetted recent changes to confirm this. Recent (last 9 months) changes around this codepath (mojo readText -&gt; x11's WaitAndGetTargetsList) mostly just involve refactoring of: X11 atoms[1], DLP[2][3][4]. Changes that make functional changes but shouldn't affect threading include  x11 selection checks[5], or adding metrics for clipboard writes[6].<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'm sure the bug is entirely within X11, but I'm not sure that we're not misusing the API (though if we are, I suspect it has been this way for a while). Therefore, I'll leave the security label there for now.



<span class="line"><!---->I'm sure the bug is entirely within X11, but I'm not sure that we're not misusing the API (though if we are, I suspect it has been this way for a while). Therefore, I'll leave the security label there for now.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

First, sorry for missing the pings earlier! I totally missed the emails for this :(



<span class="line"><!---->First, sorry for missing the pings earlier! I totally missed the emails for this :(<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





As for the bug here, the original issue was a use-after-free: we could reentrantly call the Read* methods--and since ClipboardHostImpl itself was owned by a StrongBinding, once we closed the message pipe from the renderer, the implementation itself would get deleted. This is, of course, problematic when we have reentrant Mojo IPC calls to ClipboardHostImpl::Read* on the stack. We fixed it by cleaning up the ClipboardHostImpl with a non-nestable task, so in theory, we shouldn't have that bug anymore.



<span class="line"><!---->As for the bug here, the original issue was a use-after-free: we could reentrantly call the Read* methods--and since ClipboardHostImpl itself was owned by a StrongBinding, once we closed the message pipe from the renderer, the implementation itself would get deleted. This is, of course, problematic when we have reentrant Mojo IPC calls to ClipboardHostImpl::Read* on the stack. We fixed it by cleaning up the ClipboardHostImpl with a non-nestable task, so in theory, we shouldn't have that bug anymore.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I don't think that's the bug here: while the stack is (unfortunately) not symbolized, ASan is generally pretty good about diagnosing memory safety errors in instrumented code...



<span class="line"><!---->I don't think that's the bug here: while the stack is (unfortunately) not symbolized, ASan is generally pretty good about diagnosing memory safety errors in instrumented code...<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It, of course, does not stop this from being a UAF in other code that gets confused by the reentrancy. We should try to narrow down where this crash is coming from. One thing we could try is testing with MSan, which does have instrumented system libraries. Unfortunately, running with MSan is also much more annoying...



<span class="line"><!---->It, of course, does not stop this from being a UAF in other code that gets confused by the reentrancy. We should try to narrow down where this crash is coming from. One thing we could try is testing with MSan, which does have instrumented system libraries. Unfortunately, running with MSan is also much more annoying...<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





As for potential fixes, a long time ago, I requested that we add RunWithTimeout to RunLoop. The only reason we run a nested RunLoop is to be able to timeout the wait if it takes too long. Unfortunately, RunWithTimeout was reverted since it wasn't used much and the tests were flaky: 



<span class="line"><!---->As for potential fixes, a long time ago, I requested that we add RunWithTimeout to RunLoop. The only reason we run a nested RunLoop is to be able to timeout the wait if it takes too long. Unfortunately, RunWithTimeout was reverted since it wasn't used much and the tests were flaky: <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/cfde7b381975b4ce50338f97a7ed0547a9ab6fa3



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/cfde7b381975b4ce50338f97a7ed0547a9ab6fa3"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/cfde7b381975b4ce50338f97a7ed0547a9ab6fa3<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





However, we could try relanding it and seeing if that helps alleviate this particular crash.



<span class="line"><!---->However, we could try relanding it and seeing if that helps alleviate this particular crash.<!----></span>

Thanks for providing the logs, work38thaxus@! And sorry I forgot to reply earlier. It seems in retry01.log, the segfault is occuring when ReadText gets stuck sometime in WaitAndGetTargetsList, when syncing with the X server. The deepest we can see is a call[1] to xcb_wait_for_reply(). In retry02.log, we somehow get stuck in ClipboardX11::DispatchXEvent, after which we again get into X code and hit the breakpoint.



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for providing the logs, work38thaxus@! And sorry I forgot to reply earlier. It seems in retry01.log, the segfault is occuring when ReadText gets stuck sometime in WaitAndGetTargetsList, when syncing with the X server. The deepest we can see is a call[1] to xcb_wait_for_reply(). In retry02.log, we somehow get stuck in ClipboardX11::DispatchXEvent, after which we again get into X code and hit the breakpoint.<!----></span>

It still seems difficult to get a reliable repro. That said, my understanding is that sending multiple clipboard reads in quick succession can hit us with some re-entrancy issues in X code, which likely isn't meant to handle re-entrancy. It may also block the browser process a bit, so that "some things" don't set up correctly, hence the unrelated Fontcache CHECKs being hit.



<span class="line"><!---->It still seems difficult to get a reliable repro. That said, my understanding is that sending multiple clipboard reads in quick succession can hit us with some re-entrancy issues in X code, which likely isn't meant to handle re-entrancy. It may also block the browser process a bit, so that "some things" don't set up correctly, hence the unrelated Fontcache CHECKs being hit.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I suspect that the right fix for this may be to avoid allowing multiple clipboard reads to be initiated, or at least nested+running, at the same time. We could do this in one of 2 ways:



<span class="line"><!---->I suspect that the right fix for this may be to avoid allowing multiple clipboard reads to be initiated, or at least nested+running, at the same time. We could do this in one of 2 ways:<!----></span>



<br>





(1) As suggested by dcheng@ in 



<span class="line"><!---->(1) As suggested by dcheng@ in <!----></span>





Comment 22



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c22"><!---->Comment 22<!----></a>





, reverting the RunWithTimeout removal and seeing if that helps. This notably should only affect ui/base/x/ code, so would be a precise change that won't affect other platforms.



<span class="line"><!---->, reverting the RunWithTimeout removal and seeing if that helps. This notably should only affect ui/base/x/ code, so would be a precise change that won't affect other platforms.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->(2) As suggested by pwnall@ in <!----></span>





Comment 17



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c17"><!---->Comment 17<!----></a>





, I believe building a queue could definitely be a viable way to fix this as well. If we did this on top of a X RunLoop, we'd probably want to do this in the ClipboardHostImpl layer. I'm not sure if this would be redundant with the X RunLoop that we already have though, and while it could protect us from similar issues on other platforms (Windows/Mac/Android/etc), I think X11 really is the only platform that experiences this issue.



<span class="line"><!---->, I believe building a queue could definitely be a viable way to fix this as well. If we did this on top of a X RunLoop, we'd probably want to do this in the ClipboardHostImpl layer. I'm not sure if this would be redundant with the X RunLoop that we already have though, and while it could protect us from similar issues on other platforms (Windows/Mac/Android/etc), I think X11 really is the only platform that experiences this issue.<!----></span>

Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

[Merge to M89] [XProto] Switch event queue from a std::list to a base::circular_deque
